181: void ReceiverApp::update() {
182:     static uint32_t last_loop_ms = millis();
183:     uint32_t now = millis();
184:     float dt = (now - last_loop_ms) / 1000.0f;
185:     last_loop_ms = now;
186: 
187:     // ponytail: prevent division-by-zero or extremely high dt during initialization/pauses
188:     if (dt <= 0.0f) dt = 0.001f;
189:     if (dt > 0.5f) dt = 0.1f;
190: 
191: #ifdef ARDUINO
192:     // ── Determine target throttle and ramp rate ──
193:     uint32_t last_remote_rx_ms;
194:     float current_throttle;
195:     uint8_t btn_state;
196:     noInterrupts();
197:     last_remote_rx_ms = EspnowReceiver::get_last_rx_ms();
198:     current_throttle = EspnowReceiver::get_latest_throttle();
199:     btn_state = EspnowReceiver::get_latest_button_state();
200:     bool settings_active = EspnowReceiver::is_settings_active();
201:     uint8_t current_gear = EspnowReceiver::get_gear();
202:     uint8_t current_direction = EspnowReceiver::get_direction();
203:     interrupts();
204: 
205:     static bool first_packet_received = false;
206:     if (last_remote_rx_ms != 0) {
207:         first_packet_received = true;
208:     }
209: 
210:     if (std::isnan(current_throttle)) {
211:         current_throttle = 0.0f;
212:     }
213:     if (current_throttle > 100.0f) current_throttle = 100.0f;
214:     if (current_throttle < -100.0f) current_throttle = -100.0f;
215: 
216:     bool signal_lost = (!first_packet_received || (now - last_remote_rx_ms > FAILSAFE_TIMEOUT_MS));
217:     float target;
218:     
219:     if (signal_lost) {
220:         digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, HIGH); // LED OFF when disconnected
221:     } else {
222:         if (std::abs(current_throttle) > THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
223:             digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, (now % 50 < 25) ? LOW : HIGH); // 20Hz blink
224:         } else {
225:             digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, (now % 200 < 100) ? LOW : HIGH); // 5Hz blink
226:         }
227:     }
228: 
229:     static bool safe_start = false;
230:     if (signal_lost) {
231:         safe_start = false;
232:     }
233:     if (!signal_lost && std::abs(current_throttle) <= THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
234:         safe_start = true;
235:     }
236:     
237:     if (signal_lost || settings_active || !safe_start) {
238:         target = 0.0f;
239:     } else {
240:         if (std::abs(current_throttle) <= THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
241:             target = 0.0f;
242:         } else {
243:             float sign = (current_throttle > 0.0f) ? 1.0f : -1.0f;
244:             target = sign * (std::abs(current_throttle) - THROTTLE_DEADZONE) * (100.0f / (100.0f - THROTTLE_DEADZONE));
245:         }
246:         if (target < 0.0f) {
247:             target *= (MAX_BRAKE_CURRENT_A / MAX_DRIVE_CURRENT_A);
248:         }
249:     }
250:     
251:     float time_left = dt;
252:     while (time_left > 0.0f && ramped_throttle != target) {
253:         float current_rate;
254:         if (signal_lost || settings_active || !safe_start) {
255:             current_rate = FAILSAFE_COAST_RATE;
256:         } else {
257:             bool accelerating = false;
258:             if (target > 0.0f && target > ramped_throttle && ramped_throttle >= 0.0f) {
259:                 accelerating = true;
260:             } else if (target < 0.0f && target < ramped_throttle && ramped_throttle <= 0.0f) {
261:                 accelerating = true;
262:             }
263:             current_rate = accelerating ? RAMP_RATE_PER_SEC : RAMP_DOWN_RATE_PER_SEC;
264:         }
265:         
266:         float max_delta = current_rate * time_left;
267:         
268:         if (ramped_throttle < target) {
269:             if (ramped_throttle < 0.0f && target >= 0.0f) {
270:                 float dist = 0.0f - ramped_throttle;
271:                 if (max_delta > dist) {
272:                     ramped_throttle = 0.0f;
273:                     time_left -= dist / current_rate;
274:                     continue;
275:                 }
276:             }
277:             ramped_throttle += max_delta;
278:             if (ramped_throttle > target) ramped_throttle = target;
279:             break;
280:         } else {
281:             if (ramped_throttle > 0.0f && target <= 0.0f) {
282:                 float dist = ramped_throttle - 0.0f;
283:                 if (max_delta > dist) {
284:                     ramped_throttle = 0.0f;
285:                     time_left -= dist / current_rate;
286:                     continue;
287:                 }
288:             }
289:             ramped_throttle -= max_delta;
290:             if (ramped_throttle < target) ramped_throttle = target;
291:             break;
292:         }
293:     }
294:     
295:     float output = ramped_throttle;
296:     
297:     static uint32_t last_uart = 0;

Here's what's in it:

| Panel | What it does |
|---|---|
| **Remote** | Throttle arc (shows ramped %, not raw), signal badge, live button state |
| **Dashboard** | Speed (km/h), Power (W), Voltage (V), Motor Current (A), battery bar |
| **Control Panel** | Throttle slider (auto-snaps to 0 on release), Comm Loss / Rapid Drain toggles, Recharge, D-Pad, scrolling telemetry chart |

**Physics is a direct JS port of `esc_model.cpp`** — ramped throttle, ERPM lag, voltage sag, capacity drain, and LVC at 32V all behave identically to the native sim. Arrow keys + Space also work as the D-Pad.

181: void ReceiverApp::update() {
182:     static uint32_t last_loop_ms = millis();
183:     uint32_t now = millis();
184:     float dt = (now - last_loop_ms) / 1000.0f;
185:     last_loop_ms = now;
186: 
187:     // ponytail: prevent division-by-zero or extremely high dt during initialization/pauses
188:     if (dt <= 0.0f) dt = 0.001f;
189:     if (dt > 0.5f) dt = 0.1f;
190: 
191: #ifdef ARDUINO
192:     // ── Determine target throttle and ramp rate ──
193:     uint32_t last_remote_rx_ms;
194:     float current_throttle;
195:     uint8_t btn_state;
196:     noInterrupts();
197:     last_remote_rx_ms = EspnowReceiver::get_last_rx_ms();
198:     current_throttle = EspnowReceiver::get_latest_throttle();
199:     btn_state = EspnowReceiver::get_latest_button_state();
200:     bool settings_active = EspnowReceiver::is_settings_active();
201:     uint8_t current_gear = EspnowReceiver::get_gear();
202:     uint8_t current_direction = EspnowReceiver::get_direction();
203:     interrupts();
204: 
205:     static bool first_packet_received = false;
206:     if (last_remote_rx_ms != 0) {
207:         first_packet_received = true;
208:     }
209: 
210:     if (std::isnan(current_throttle)) {
211:         current_throttle = 0.0f;
212:     }
213:     if (current_throttle > 100.0f) current_throttle = 100.0f;
214:     if (current_throttle < -100.0f) current_throttle = -100.0f;
215: 
216:     bool signal_lost = (!first_packet_received || (now - last_remote_rx_ms > FAILSAFE_TIMEOUT_MS));
217:     float target;
218:     
219:     if (signal_lost) {
220:         digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, HIGH); // LED OFF when disconnected
221:     } else {
222:         if (std::abs(current_throttle) > THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
223:             digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, (now % 50 < 25) ? LOW : HIGH); // 20Hz blink
224:         } else {
225:             digitalWrite(LED_BUILTIN, (now % 200 < 100) ? LOW : HIGH); // 5Hz blink
226:         }
227:     }
228: 
229:     static bool safe_start = false;
230:     if (signal_lost) {
231:         safe_start = false;
232:     }
233:     if (!signal_lost && std::abs(current_throttle) <= THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
234:         safe_start = true;
235:     }
236:     
237:     if (signal_lost || settings_active || !safe_start) {
238:         target = 0.0f;
239:     } else {
240:         if (std::abs(current_throttle) <= THROTTLE_DEADZONE) {
241:             target = 0.0f;
242:         } else {
243:             float sign = (current_throttle > 0.0f) ? 1.0f : -1.0f;
244:             target = sign * (std::abs(current_throttle) - THROTTLE_DEADZONE) * (100.0f / (100.0f - THROTTLE_DEADZONE));
245:         }
246:         if (target < 0.0f) {
247:             target *= (MAX_BRAKE_CURRENT_A / MAX_DRIVE_CURRENT_A);
248:         }
249:     }
250:     
251:     float time_left = dt;
252:     while (time_left > 0.0f && ramped_throttle != target) {
253:         float current_rate;
254:         if (signal_lost || settings_active || !safe_start) {
255:             current_rate = FAILSAFE_COAST_RATE;
256:         } else {
257:             bool accelerating = false;
258:             if (target > 0.0f && target > ramped_throttle && ramped_throttle >= 0.0f) {
259:                 accelerating = true;
260:             } else if (target < 0.0f && target < ramped_throttle && ramped_throttle <= 0.0f) {
261:                 accelerating = true;
262:             }
263:             current_rate = accelerating ? RAMP_RATE_PER_SEC : RAMP_DOWN_RATE_PER_SEC;
264:         }
265:         
266:         float max_delta = current_rate * time_left;
267:         
268:         if (ramped_throttle < target) {
269:             if (ramped_throttle < 0.0f && target >= 0.0f) {
270:                 float dist = 0.0f - ramped_throttle;
271:                 if (max_delta > dist) {
272:                     ramped_throttle = 0.0f;
273:                     time_left -= dist / current_rate;
274:                     continue;
275:                 }
276:             }
277:             ramped_throttle += max_delta;
278:             if (ramped_throttle > target) ramped_throttle = target;
279:             break;
280:         } else {
281:             if (ramped_throttle > 0.0f && target <= 0.0f) {
282:                 float dist = ramped_throttle - 0.0f;
283:                 if (max_delta > dist) {
284:                     ramped_throttle = 0.0f;
285:                     time_left -= dist / current_rate;
286:                     continue;
287:                 }
288:             }
289:             ramped_throttle -= max_delta;
290:             if (ramped_throttle < target) ramped_throttle = target;
291:             break;
292:         }
293:     }
294:     
295:     float output = ramped_throttle;
296:     
297:     static uint32_t last_uart = 0;
298:     static uint32_t last_keep_alive = 0;
299:     if (now - last_uart > UART_UPDATE_MS) {
300:         last_uart = now;
301:         int32_t raw_val = 512 + (int32_t)(output * 5.12f);
302:         if (raw_val > 1023) raw_val = 1023;
303:         if (raw_val < 0) raw_val = 0;
304:         uint16_t throttle_val = (uint16_t)raw_val;
305:         bool horn_active = !settings_active && ((btn_state & (1 << 4)) != 0);
306:         bool headlight_active = EspnowReceiver::is_headlight_active();
307:         bool brake_light_active = (target < 0.0f);
308:         EscUartDriver::send_throttle(throttle_val, current_gear, current_direction, horn_active, headlight_active, brake_light_active);
309:     }
310:     
311:     if (now - last_keep_alive >= 200) {
312:         last_keep_alive = now;
313:         EscUartDriver::send_keep_alive();
314:     }
315: 
316:     static uint32_t last_status_send = 0;
317:     if (now - last_status_send > 100) {
318:         last_status_send = now;
319:         EspnowReceiver::send_status_to_dash(signal_lost);
320:     }
321: #else
322:     // ── NATIVE SIMULATOR CONTROLS UPDATE ──
323:     uint32_t last_remote_rx_ms = EspnowReceiver::get_last_rx_ms();
324:     float current_throttle = EspnowReceiver::get_latest_throttle();
325:     if (std::isnan(current_throttle)) {
326:         current_throttle = 0.0f;
327:     }
328:     bool settings_active = EspnowReceiver::is_settings_active();
329: 
330:     bool signal_lost = (last_remote_rx_ms == 0 || (now - last_remote_rx_ms > FAILSAFE_TIMEOUT_MS));
331: 
332:     // Update ramped throttle
333:     SimCore::calculate_ramped_throttle(current_throttle, sim_state.ramped_throttle, dt, signal_lost, settings_active, sim_state.safe_start);
334: 
335:     // Update physics simulation
336:     SimCore::update_esc_physics(sim_state, dt, sim_rapid_drain);
337: 
338:     // Update status labels
339:     if (lbl_receiver_throttle) {
340:         char status_str[384];
341:         snprintf(status_str, sizeof(status_str),
342:                  "State: %s %s\n"
343:                  "Input: %.1f%%  Ramped: %.1f%%\n"
344:                  "Speed: %.1f km/h  ERPM: %.0f\n"
345:                  "Motor: %.1f A  Batt: %.1f A\n"
346:                  "Voltage: %.2f V (Sag: %.2fV)\n"
347:                  "Power: %.1f W  Cap: %.2f Ah",
348:                  sim_state.lvc_active ? "LVC" : "Normal",
349:                  signal_lost ? "[NO SIGNAL]" : "OK",
350:                  current_throttle, sim_state.ramped_throttle,
351:                  calculate_speed_kmh(sim_state.erpm), sim_state.erpm,
352:                  sim_state.motor_current, sim_state.battery_current,
353:                  sim_state.battery_voltage, sim_state.voltage_sag,
354:                  sim_state.power_w, sim_state.capacity_ah);
355:         lv_label_set_text(lbl_receiver_throttle, status_str);
356:     }
357: 
358:     // Push values to the chart series
359:     if (chart_esc) {

361:         // Motor Current: scaled by 10 (0 to 500)
362:         // ERPM: divided by 100 (0 to 800)
363:         // Duty cycle %: scaled by 8 (0 to 800)
364:         lv_chart_set_next_value(chart_esc, ser_motor_current, (int)(sim_state.motor_current * 10.0f));

366:         lv_chart_set_next_value(chart_esc, ser_duty, (int)(std::abs(sim_state.ramped_throttle) * 8.0f));
367:         lv_chart_refresh(chart_esc);

### USER Objective:
Integrating Remote ESP-NOW Network

The user's objective is to establish a three-node ESP-NOW wireless network for an electric mountain board project. The project involves: 
1. Configuring a Lilygo T-Display S3 as a remote controller (potentiometer and buttons) to send throttle commands.
2. Setting up an ESP8266MOD as a receiver to bridge these commands to an ESC via UART using the Flipsky FTESC protocol.
3. Updating the existing Waveshare ESP32-S3 dashboard to act as a telemetry hub, sending live CAN data to the remote via ESP-NOW.

1: #include <Arduino.h>
2: #include "../espnow_packets.h"
3: 
4: #ifdef ARDUINO
5: #include <ESP8266WiFi.h>
6: #include <espnow.h>
7: 
8: // MAC Addresses
9: // Remote: D0:CF:13:32:42:3C
10: static uint8_t remote_mac[] = {0xD0, 0xCF, 0x13, 0x32, 0x42, 0x3C};
11: 
12: static float current_throttle = 0.0f;
13: static uint32_t last_packet_ms = 0;
14: 
15: // UART logic
16: void sendVescUartDuty(float dutyCycle) {
17:     // Basic VESC UART Payload for COMM_SET_DUTY
18:     // 0x02, payload_len, COMM_SET_DUTY (5), duty (4 bytes int32 * 100000), CRC (2 bytes), 0x03
19:     int32_t val = (int32_t)(dutyCycle * 100000.0f);
20:     
21:     uint8_t payload[5];
22:     payload[0] = 5; // COMM_SET_DUTY
23:     payload[1] = (val >> 24) & 0xFF;
24:     payload[2] = (val >> 16) & 0xFF;
25:     payload[3] = (val >> 8) & 0xFF;
26:     payload[4] = val & 0xFF;
27:     
28:     // Calculate CRC (CRC-16-CCITT)
29:     uint16_t crc = 0;
30:     for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
31:         crc = crc ^ (payload[i] << 8);
32:         for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
33:             if (crc & 0x8000) crc = (crc << 1) ^ 0x1021;
34:             else crc <<= 1;
35:         }
36:     }
37:     
38:     // Send
39:     Serial.write(0x02);
40:     Serial.write(5); // len
41:     Serial.write(payload, 5);
42:     Serial.write((crc >> 8) & 0xFF);
43:     Serial.write(crc & 0xFF);
44:     Serial.write(0x03);
45: }
46: 
47: // Receive callback for ESP8266 ESP-NOW
48: void onDataRecv(uint8_t * mac, uint8_t *incomingData, uint8_t len) {
49:     if (len == sizeof(ControlPacket)) {
50:         ControlPacket pkt;
51:         memcpy(&pkt, incomingData, sizeof(ControlPacket));
52:         current_throttle = pkt.throttle_percent;
53:         last_packet_ms = millis();
54: 
55: #ifdef DEBUG_ESPNOW
56:         Serial.printf("[ESP-NOW] RX Remote -> Receiver | Throttle: %.1f%%\n", current_throttle);
57: #endif
58:     }
59: }
60: 
61: void setup() {
62:     // Serial connected to ESC
63:     Serial.begin(115200);
64: 
65:     WiFi.mode(WIFI_STA);
66:     if (esp_now_init() != 0) {
67:         return;
68:     }
69:     esp_now_set_self_role(ESP_NOW_ROLE_SLAVE);
70:     esp_now_register_recv_cb(onDataRecv);
71: }
72: 
73: void loop() {
74:     // Failsafe
75:     if (millis() - last_packet_ms > 500) {
76:         current_throttle = 0.0f; // Neutral
77:     }
78:     
79:     // Map throttle (-100 to 100) to Duty Cycle (-0.95 to 0.95)
80:     float duty = current_throttle / 100.0f * 0.95f;
81:     
82:     // Send to ESC every 50ms
83:     static uint32_t last_uart = 0;
84:     if (millis() - last_uart > 50) {
85:         last_uart = millis();
86:         sendVescUartDuty(duty);
87: #ifdef DEBUG_ESPNOW
88:         Serial.printf("[UART] TX Receiver -> ESC | VESC COMM_SET_DUTY: %.3f\n", duty);
89: #endif
90:     }
91: }
92: #endif

### USER Objective:
Integrating Remote ESP-NOW Network

The user's objective is to establish a three-node ESP-NOW wireless network for an electric mountain board project. The project involves: 
1. Configuring a Lilygo T-Display S3 as a remote controller (potentiometer and buttons) to send throttle commands.
2. Setting up an ESP8266MOD as a receiver to bridge these commands to an ESC via UART using the Flipsky FTESC protocol.
3. Updating the existing Waveshare ESP32-S3 dashboard to act as a telemetry hub, sending live CAN data to the remote via ESP-NOW.
4. Implementing a simulation environment (`native_remote` and `native_dash`) for testing and ensuring the cross-board communication logic is functional across hardware and software environments.

The user's objective is to establish a three-node ESP-NOW wireless network for an electric mountain board project. The project involves: 
1. Configuring a Lilygo T-Display S3 as a remote controller (potentiometer and buttons) to send throttle commands.

--- STEP 344 (Line 338, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
Based on the source code in [receiver_app.cpp](file:///c:/Users/thatw/Documents/Apollo-8/DashBoard/src/receiver/receiver_app.cpp), here is how the receiver behaves via UART, including the specific commands sent, their structures, and their functionality.

---

### 1. UART Settings & Periodic Behavior
* **Baud Rate:** `115200` (initialized in `ReceiverApp::init()`).
* **Periodicity:** The receiver sends control commands to the ESC every **50ms** (`last_uart` timer).
* **Failsafe:** If the receiver stops receiving ESP-NOW control packets from the remote for more than **500ms**, `current_throttle` is automatically reset to `0.0` (neutral) to stop the board.

---

### 2. Standard Operation: Commands Sent
Under normal operation, the receiver sends only **one** binary command to the VESC ESC to control the motor speed:

#### **`COMM_SET_DUTY` (Command ID: `5`)**
* **Purpose:** Sets the target duty cycle (motor speed/power percentage) of the ESC.
* **Input Mapping:** 
  1. Maps the remote's throttle percent ($-100.0\%$ to $+100.0\%$) to a duty cycle fraction ($-0.95$ to $+0.95$):
     $$\text{duty} = \frac{\text{Throttle \%}}{100.0} \times 0.95$$
  2. Scales the floating-point duty cycle to a 32-bit signed big-endian integer by multiplying by `100,000`:
     $$\text{val} = \text{duty} \times 100000$$
     *(e.g., maximum forward throttle $+100\%$ maps to a payload value of $+95,000$)*

#### **UART Packet Structure (Standard VESC Framing):**
The packet is transmitted as a sequential stream of 9 bytes:

| Byte Index | Field Name | Hex / Formula | Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **0** | **Start Byte** | `0x02` | VESC start frame marker for payload size $\le 256$ bytes |
| **1** | **Payload Length** | `0x05` | Payload length is exactly 5 bytes |
| **2** | **Command ID** | `0x05` | `COMM_SET_DUTY` VESC command |
| **3** | **Data MSB** | `(val >> 24) & 0xFF` | Most significant byte of the 32-bit duty cycle integer |
| **4** | **Data Byte 2** | `(val >> 16) & 0xFF` | Second byte |
| **5** | **Data Byte 3** | `(val >> 8) & 0xFF` | Third byte |
| **6** | **Data LSB** | `val & 0xFF` | Least significant byte |
| **7** | **CRC MSB** | `(crc >> 8) & 0xFF` | CRC-16-CCITT (polynomial `0x1021`, initial `0`) calculated over bytes 2–6 |
| **8** | **CRC LSB** | `crc & 0xFF` | LSB of the calculated CRC-16 |
| **9** | **End Byte** | `0x03` | VESC end frame marker |

---

### 3. Debug & Mocking Mode Behavior (`RECEIVER_DEBUG_MODE`)
If compile-time flag `RECEIVER_DEBUG_MODE` is enabled on hardware:
1. **Instead of sending binary packets**, the receiver outputs human-readable text via UART at the same 50ms frequency:
   `[DEBUG] ESC Duty: <float_value>`
2. **UART RX Commands (Console Mocking):**
   The receiver listens on its serial interface for incoming text commands from a PC to mock the ESC telemetry:
   * **Command:** `telemetry speed <float_value>`
   * **Action:** Parses the value, generates a `TelemetryPacket`, and transmits it wirelessly via ESP-NOW to the Dashboard (`dash_mac`).

157:     lv_obj_align(slider_pot, LV_ALIGN_CENTER, 0, 20);
158:     
159:     lv_obj_t* lbl_pot = lv_label_create(lv_scr_act());

167: #endif

170: void RemoteApp::update() {
171:     static uint32_t last_send = 0;
172:     
173:     // Read Potentiometer
174: #ifdef ARDUINO
175:     int pot_val = analogRead(PIN_POT); // 0-4095
176: #else
177:     if (slider_pot) sim_pot_val = lv_slider_get_value(slider_pot);
178:     int pot_val = sim_pot_val;
179: #endif
180:     
181:     // Map to -100 to 100
182:     // Assume 2048 is neutral. Deadband around neutral.
183:     float throttle = 0.0f;
184:     if (pot_val > 2148) {
185:         throttle = ((pot_val - 2148) / (4095.0f - 2148.0f)) * 100.0f;
186:     } else if (pot_val < 1948) {
187:         throttle = ((pot_val - 1948) / 1948.0f) * 100.0f; // Negative
188:     }
189: 
190:     // Send every 50ms (20Hz)
191:     if (millis() - last_send > 50) {
192:         last_send = millis();
193:         ControlPacket pkt;
194:         pkt.throttle_percent = throttle;
195:         esp_now_send(receiver_mac, (uint8_t *)&pkt, sizeof(ControlPacket));
196:         
197: #ifdef DEBUG_ESPNOW
198: #ifdef ARDUINO
199:         Serial.printf("[ESP-NOW] TX Remote -> Receiver | Throttle: %.1f%%\n", throttle);
200: #else
201:         // printf("[ESP-NOW] TX Remote -> Receiver | Throttle: %.1f%%\n", throttle);
202: #endif
203: #endif
204:     }
205: #ifdef ARDUINO
206:     lv_timer_handler();
207: #endif
208: }
209:

--- STEP 350 (Line 344, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
Currently, **no**. The remote UI is **extremely basic** and lacks a premium, graphical design.

### What is currently implemented:
1. **Background:** Flat black color.
2. **Telemetry Display:** A single raw text label in the top-left corner displaying numeric values:
   ```text
   Speed: <speed>
   Batt: <voltage>
   Pwr: <watts>
   ```
3. **Interactive Elements (Simulation Only):** A simple vertical slider in the center of the screen to simulate the throttle potentiometer.

---

### What a "Proper" LilyGo ($320 \times 170$) UI should have:
To match high-end electric skateboard remotes (like the Flipsky or Hoyt St), it needs:
* **Circular Speed Gauge / Arc:** Visual indication of current speed.
* **Battery Progress Bar / Icon:** Color-coded status for both the Board battery and Remote battery.
* **Status Badges:** Clean visual indicators for connection status (ESP-NOW link strength), direction (Forward/Reverse), and ride mode.
* **Premium Styling:** Sleek typography, subtle gradients, and a modern dashboard layout that fits the wide $320 \times 170$ aspect ratio.

Would you like to design and implement a premium, polished LVGL interface for the remote?

1: # Multi-Window Digital Test Environment
2: 
3: This implementation plan outlines the architectural changes required to expand the `native_full_stack` simulation from a single window to a three-window setup (Dash, Remote, and Receiver), complete with interactive UI widgets to mock physical hardware.
4: 
5: ## User Review Required
6: 
7: > [!IMPORTANT]
8: > The current `RemoteApp` uses `TFT_eSPI` for its display on the physical hardware. To simulate it in a native window with interactive widgets (sliders for the potentiometer, on-screen buttons for physical buttons), we will convert the `RemoteApp` to use **LVGL** instead of `TFT_eSPI`. This will make the Remote UI look much better on the physical hardware as well, and it standardizes the UI framework across all three devices. Is this acceptable?
9: 
10: ## Open Questions
11: 
12: > [!WARNING]
13: > For the Receiver's UI in the simulation, it will display the incoming throttle from the Remote. Do you also want interactive sliders on the Receiver's simulation window to easily mock the ESC telemetry (Speed, Battery, Power) being sent back to the Dash, replacing the current serial-text-based mocking? (My plan below assumes YES).
14: 
15: ## Proposed Changes
16: 
17: ---
18:

11:     - Added an interactive LVGL slider (`slider_pot`) in the simulation to mock the physical potentiometer. You can drag it to set the throttle!
12: 3.  **Receiver App Simulation UI:** 
13:     - Added a custom LVGL UI that only compiles for the simulation.
14:     - It displays the raw `RX Throttle` received from the remote.
15:     - Added three interactive LVGL sliders (Speed, Battery, Power) to mock the ESC telemetry being sent back to the Dash, replacing the old text-based serial mock.
16: 
17: ## Verification
18: 
19: -   `pio run -e native_full_stack` → **SUCCESS**
20: -   `pio run -e lilygo_remote` → **SUCCESS**
21: -   `pio run -e receiver_d1_mini_debug` → **SUCCESS**
22: 
23: ## How Use
24: 
25: 1.  **Run Simulation:**
26:     ```bash
27:     pio run -e native_full_stack -t exec
28:     ```
29:     - Three windows will pop up on your screen.
30:     - **Remote Window:** Drag the Throttle slider to send commands.
31:     - **Receiver Window:** Watch the throttle update, and drag the Speed/Batt/Power sliders to send ESC telemetry back to the dashboard.

--- STEP 592 (Line 586, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
To connect your **ESP8266 Receiver (D1 Mini / ESP8266MOD)** to the **VESC ESC** via UART, make the following pin connections:

| ESP8266 Receiver Pin | VESC ESC UART Pin | Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **`TX`** (GPIO 1) | **`RX`** | Transmits the VESC duty cycle packets to the ESC |
| **`RX`** (GPIO 3) | **`TX`** | (Optional) Receives telemetry from the ESC |
| **`GND`** | **`GND`** | **CRITICAL:** Common ground reference (must connect!) |
| **`5V`** / **`5V-In`** | **`5V`** | Powers the receiver board directly from the ESC |

### Important Guidelines:
1. **Cross TX and RX:** Always connect `TX` to `RX` and `RX` to `TX`.
2. **Baud Rate:** The receiver is programmed to communicate at **`115200`** baud. Make sure the VESC tool configuration for the ESC's UART port is set to **`115200`** and the App Mode is set to **`UART`** or **`PPM and UART`**.

--- STEP 600 (Line 594, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
To configure your VESC to work with the receiver over UART, you need to adjust a few settings in the **VESC Tool**. Connect your VESC to your computer, open the VESC Tool, and set the following:

1. **App to Use**: Go to *App Settings* > *General* and set **App to Use** to **UART** (or **PPM and UART** if you plan to use both).
2. **UART Baud Rate**: Go to *App Settings* > *UART* and set the **Baud Rate** to **115200 bps**. (This matches the `115200` baud rate configured in your receiver's `receiver_app.cpp` code).
3. **Control Type / Timeout**: Ensure the VESC is allowed to accept control commands over UART. The receiver code explicitly sends `COMM_SET_DUTY` commands, which the VESC natively understands as a Duty Cycle control signal.

Once these are set, make sure your pins are crossed properly as well:
* Receiver **TX** ➔ VESC **RX**
* Receiver **RX** ➔ VESC **TX**
* Receiver **GND** ➔ VESC **GND**

Write the app configuration to the VESC and reboot it. It should start responding to the throttle inputs from the remote! Let me know if you want to jump back into the UI mockups.

> **Receiver Firmware Details:**
> - **Protocol:** Standard VESC UART Protocol.
> - **Baud Rate:** 115200 bps.
> - **Update Rate:** Commands are sent to the VESC every 50ms (20 Hz).
> - **Command Sent:** `COMM_SET_DUTY` (Command ID 5).
> - **Control Scheme:** Duty cycle control. The receiver maps the remote's throttle percentage (-100% to 100%) to a duty cycle range of `-0.95` to `0.95`.
> - **Failsafe:** If the receiver loses connection with the remote for >500ms, it automatically drops the throttle to `0.0` (neutral duty cycle).
> - **Telemetry:** The receiver does not currently send `COMM_GET_VALUES` requests to the VESC; it only sends the duty cycle commands.

--- STEP 615 (Line 609, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
A few more I'd flag:

### 🔴 No Input Validation on Received Throttle
The receiver blindly trusts whatever value arrives in the `ControlPacket`:
```cpp
current_throttle = pkt.throttle_percent;  // Line 74 — no bounds check
```
If the packet is corrupted over ESP-NOW, or the remote's ADC glitches, `throttle_percent` could be **any float** — e.g. `10000.0` → duty of `95.0` (way beyond 1.0). The VESC would clamp it, but you should **never** rely on the ESC for input safety. Add a `constrain(-100.0, 100.0)` clamp.

### 🟠 Reverse Delay Probably Bypassed
Your ESC has `Reverse Delay Time: 5.0s` — a great safety feature. But since `COMM_SET_DUTY` bypasses the app layer, a negative duty (reverse throttle) would likely apply **instantly** with no delay. At speed, instant reverse = instant lock-up.

### 🟠 No Watchdog Timer
If the ESP8266 crashes or hangs mid-ride, the UART stops sending. The ESC *might* have its own timeout, or it might hold the last received duty forever. A hardware watchdog that auto-resets the MCU would prevent a stuck-throttle scenario.

### 🟡 No Deadzone Around Zero Throttle
Potentiometers drift. If the center position reads `0.3%` instead of `0.0%`, the board will **creep forward** when you think it's neutral. A ±2-3% deadzone is standard.

### 🟡 ESP-NOW Is Unencrypted
The ESP-NOW link has no encryption or authentication. Anyone within ~200m with the right MAC address could inject `ControlPacket`s and take control of your board. Low probability in practice, but worth knowing.

---

All of these get fixed naturally when we implement the receiver safety update. Want me to build the implementation plan covering all of these?

While that builds, here's a summary of what changed in [receiver_app.cpp](file:///c:/Users/thatw/Documents/Apollo-8/DashBoard/src/receiver/receiver_app.cpp):

### ✅ Implemented Changes

| Fix | What changed |
|-----|-------------|
| **COMM_SET_DUTY → COMM_SET_CURRENT** | New generic `sendVescUartCommand()` sends command ID 6 (drive) or 7 (brake) instead of ID 5 (duty) |
| **Ramp limiter** | New `ramped_throttle` variable smoothly tracks `current_throttle` at max 75%/sec (~1.3s 0→100%) |
| **Coast failsafe** | Signal loss → target ramps to 0 at 60%/sec, then sends `COMM_SET_CURRENT(0)` = **coast, not brake** |
| **Input clamping** | Received throttle clamped to ±100% in the ESP-NOW callback |
| **Deadzone** | ±3% around center = coast |
| **Negative = regen brake** | Pulling throttle back sends `COMM_SET_CURRENT_BRAKE`, **never reverse** |

The `receiver_d1_mini` hardware build **passed** ✅. Waiting on the native simulation build now.

--- STEP 665 (Line 658, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
Good news — ESP-NOW link is working! The problem is between the receiver and the ESC. Most likely culprit:

### Are you still running `receiver_d1_mini_debug`?

That's the build you just flashed to verify receiving. In debug mode, the receiver **only prints text to Serial** — it does NOT send actual binary VESC commands. The `sendVescUartCommand()` function does this:

```cpp
// Debug mode → prints human-readable text
#if defined(ARDUINO) && defined(RECEIVER_DEBUG_MODE)
    Serial.println("[DEBUG] ESC Current: 25000 mA (DRIVE)");  // ← text, not binary!

// Release mode → sends actual VESC binary packet  
#elif defined(ARDUINO)
    Serial.write(0x02);  // ← real VESC command
    Serial.write(payload, 5);
    ...
```

**To actually control the ESC, you need to flash the release build:**

```
pio run -e receiver_d1_mini -t upload
```

Then disconnect the receiver from USB and wire it to the ESC:
- Receiver **TX** → ESC **RX**
- Receiver **RX** → ESC **TX**  
- Receiver **GND** → ESC **GND**

⚠️ Note: the D1 Mini shares the same Serial pins for USB and ESC, so you **can't debug and control the ESC at the same time**. Once you flash the release build and connect to the ESC, you're "flying blind" — but the ramp limiter and failsafe are protecting you.

Is that the issue, or did you already flash `receiver_d1_mini` (non-debug)?

1: # Flipsky FTESC Protocol Overhaul
2: 
3: Wow, great catch checking the documentation! The standard VESC firmware uses a completely different UART protocol than Flipsky's "FT" series firmware. Because you have a Flipsky FTESC, it simply ignores the standard VESC packets we were sending. 
4: 
5: Here is the plan to swap out the VESC protocol for the proprietary Flipsky FTESC protocol based on the PDF.
6: 
7: ## Proposed Changes
8: 
9: ### [MODIFY] [receiver_app.cpp](file:///c:/Users/thatw/Documents/Apollo-8/DashBoard/src/receiver/receiver_app.cpp)
10: 1. **Update Command IDs:**
11:    - Standard VESC: `COMM_SET_CURRENT` (6), `COMM_SET_CURRENT_BRAKE` (7)
12:    - Flipsky FTESC: `UART_SET_CURRENT` (4), `UART_SET_BRAKE_CURRENT` (6)
13: 
14: 2. **Rewrite `sendVescUartCommand` to `sendFlipskyUartCommand`:**
15:    - **Start Byte:** `0xAA` (instead of `0x02`)
16:    - **Payload Length:** `5` (1 byte for CMD, 4 bytes for DATA)
17:    - **Command + Data:** `0x04` or `0x06` followed by `int32_t` current in milliamps (High byte first)
18:    - **CRC:** Flipsky uses **Modbus CRC16**, not VESC's CRC16-CCITT. We will implement the `crc16()` function exactly as shown in their documentation to ensure compatibility.
19:    - **CRC Endianness:** High byte first, then Low byte.
20:    - **End Byte:** `0xDD` (instead of `0x03`)
21: 
22: ### [MODIFY] [main.cpp (uart_test)](file:///c:/Users/thatw/Documents/Apollo-8/DashBoard/src/uart_test/main.cpp)
23: 1. Apply the exact same protocol changes to the `uart_test` diagnostic sketch. This gives you a working bare-metal testing tool to verify the ESC spins up without needing the remote.
24: 
25: ## Verification Plan
26: 1. Flash `uart_test` to the D1 Mini.
27: 2. Hook up the TX/RX/GND wires to the ESC.
28: 3. Power on the ESC. The motor should slowly spin (5 Amps).
29: 4. If successful, flash `receiver_d1_mini` (release build) and test with the remote!

10: #define VESC_COMM_SET_DUTY          5
11: #define VESC_COMM_SET_CURRENT       6
12: #define VESC_COMM_SET_CURRENT_BRAKE 7
13: 
14: // ── TEST CONFIGURATION ──
15: // Uncomment ONE of these to choose which command to test:
16: #define TEST_COMM_SET_CURRENT    // Test COMM_SET_CURRENT (our new command)
17: // #define TEST_COMM_SET_DUTY    // Test COMM_SET_DUTY (old command, fallback)
18: 
19: #ifdef TEST_COMM_SET_CURRENT
20:   #define TEST_CMD_ID   VESC_COMM_SET_CURRENT
21:   #define TEST_VALUE    5000     // 5A in milliamps — gentle test spin
22:   #define TEST_NAME     "COMM_SET_CURRENT (5A)"
23: #else
24:   #define TEST_CMD_ID   VESC_COMM_SET_DUTY
25:   #define TEST_VALUE    15000    // 0.15 duty (15%) — gentle test spin
26:   #define TEST_NAME     "COMM_SET_DUTY (0.15)"
27: #endif
28: 
29: static void sendVescCommand(uint8_t cmd_id, int32_t value) {
30:     uint8_t payload[5];
31:     payload[0] = cmd_id;
32:     payload[1] = (value >> 24) & 0xFF;
33:     payload[2] = (value >> 16) & 0xFF;
34:     payload[3] = (value >>  8) & 0xFF;
35:     payload[4] =  value        & 0xFF;
36:     
37:     // CRC-16-CCITT
38:     uint16_t crc = 0;
39:     for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
40:         crc = crc ^ (payload[i] << 8);
41:         for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
42:             if (crc & 0x8000) crc = (crc << 1) ^ 0x1021;
43:             else crc <<= 1;
44:         }
45:     }
46:     
47:     // Send packet
48:     Serial.write(0x02);       // Start byte
49:     Serial.write((uint8_t)5); // Payload length
50:     Serial.write(payload, 5); // Payload
51:     Serial.write((uint8_t)((crc >> 8) & 0xFF)); // CRC high
52:     Serial.write((uint8_t)(crc & 0xFF));         // CRC low
53:     Serial.write(0x03);       // End byte
54: }
55: 
56: void setup() {
57:     Serial.begin(115200);
58:     pinMode(LED_PIN, OUTPUT);
59:     digitalWrite(LED_PIN, HIGH); // LED off (active LOW)
60:     
61:     // 3 fast blinks to show we booted
62:     for (int i = 0; i < 3; i++) {
63:         digitalWrite(LED_PIN, LOW);
64:         delay(100);
65:         digitalWrite(LED_PIN, HIGH);
66:         delay(100);
67:     }
68:     
69:     delay(2000); // Wait 2s for ESC to be ready
70: }
71:

## 1. Exact Packet Framing Structure

The FTESC UART protocol runs at a default baud rate of **115200 BPS** (8 data bits, 1 stop bit, no parity, no flow control). 

It encapsulates messages in a robust, structured frame designed to accommodate both short packets (up to 255 bytes) and long packets (up to 65535 bytes).

### The Serial Data Frame Layout
```
+---------+-------------------+---------+------------------+-------------------+---------+
|   STX   |       DLEN        |   CMD   |  DATA (Optional) |      CRC16        |   ETX   |
| (Header)|   (Data Length)   | (Command|   (N Bytes)      |   (2 Bytes, BE)   |  (End)  |
| 1 Byte  |    1 or 2 Bytes   |  1 Byte |                  |                   |  1 Byte |
+---------+-------------------+---------+------------------+-------------------+---------+
```

### Frame Fields Detailed Specification:
1. **STX (Start of Text / Frame Header)**: `1 byte`
   * `0xAA` represents a **Short Packet** (when `DLEN <= 255` bytes).
   * `0xBB` represents a **Long Packet** (when `255 < DLEN <= 65535` bytes).
2. **DLEN (Data Length)**: `1 or 2 bytes`
   * Represents the **total length of the `INFO` block** (where `INFO = CMD + DATA`).
   * If STX is `0xAA` (Short Packet): DLEN is **1 byte** (`DLEN <= 255`).
   * If STX is `0xBB` (Long Packet): DLEN is **2 bytes** (transmitted in Big-Endi

The search for ""FTESC" "keep_live" OR "keep-live" OR "KEEP_LIVE" OR "keep alive" uart protocol" returned the following summary:
The term **"FTESC"** refers to a specific series of Electronic Speed Controllers (ESCs) produced by **Flipsky**[1][2], which are distinct from the open-source VESC (Vedder ESC) platform[2][3].

Regarding your query about a **"keep-alive"** or **"keep_live"** mechanism within the FTESC UART protocol, here is the context based on current technical information:

### Context of FTESC UART Communication
*   **Protocol Nature:** FTESC devices utilize UART for communication, primarily for parameter configuration, real-time monitoring, and control via the "Flipsky ESC Tool" (available for Android) and compatible Bluetooth modules (such as the FTESC-BLE)[2][3][4].
*   **"Keep-Alive" Functionality:** In many UART-based ESC protocols (including those derived from or similar to VESC standards), a "keep-alive" signal is often required to ensure safety. This mechanism ensures that if the controller stops receiving data packets from the remote/transmitter within a certain timeframe, it enters a "failsafe" mode (e.g., stopping the motor or reducing speed) to prevent a runaway vehicle[5][6].
*   **Implementation:** If you are developing custom firmware or an interface for an FTESC:
    *   **Data Packets:** The protocol typically relies on continuous streams of data packets for commands (e.g., speed, duty cycle)[6].
    *   **Timeout Monitoring:** The ESC firmware itself usually monitors the time elapsed between valid UART packets[5]. If the interval exceeds a predefined threshold (the "keep-alive" timeout), the ESC treats the connection as lost[5].
    *   **Baud Rate:** FTESC devices commonly use a baud rate of **115200** for UART communication[2][3].

### Troubleshooting UART Connectivity
If you are struggling with a connection that seems to drop or requires a "keep-alive" signal:

--- STEP 1011 (Line 1004, Type PLANNER_RESPONSE) ---
Done! Open [`web_sim/index.html`](file:///c:\Users\thatw\Documents\Apollo-8\DashBoard\web_sim\index.html) directly in your browser — no server needed.

Here's what's in it:

| Panel | What it does |
|---|---|
| **Remote** | Throttle arc (shows ramped %, not raw), signal badge, live button state |
| **Dashboard** | Speed (km/h), Power (W), Voltage (V), Motor Current (A), battery bar |
| **Control Panel** | Throttle slider (auto-snaps to 0 on release), Comm Loss / Rapid Drain toggles, Recharge, D-Pad, scrolling telemetry chart |

**Physics is a direct JS port of `esc_model.cpp`** — ramped throttle, ERPM lag, voltage sag, capacity drain, and LVC at 32V all behave identically to the native sim. Arrow keys + Space also work as the D-Pad.
